URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS154299309	2017-05-15 17:30:19	2316	species	White-winged Dove	Zenaida asiatica			2				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Clark	US-NV-003		33	USFWS_591		Desert NWR--Corn Creek (Field Station)	L168656	H	36.4387970	-115.3595660	2012-05-05	05:30:00	obsr235247	S10838974	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	420	3.219		2	1		0	1	0		Experienced an absolutely amazing migrant fallout on 5/5 at Corn Creek just north of Las Vegas.  David Donsker and I arrived at Corn Creek at first light and immediately noticed a number of kingbirds flying into the trees from the desert.  As the steady stream of birds continued, we noticed numerous warblers flying in along with the kingbirds.  The first tree we reached was loaded with Western Kingbirds, although only 10 feet tall it had at least 50 kingbirds on it perched like Christmas tree ornaments.  Each binocular field in each mulberry tree contained at least 5 Bullock's Orioles and a few more Western Kingbirds.  Groups of 5 to 10 warblers (mostly Audubon's) were in the trees, on the ground, in the grass, on fence posts - just everywhere.  We birded the oasis from 5:15 to 11 and conservatively estimated 2,000 birds of 75 species.  Counting was next to impossible as the birds were constantly flitting from tree to tree.  We returned and birded the area again from 2:30 to 5:30, and although activity was much lower, there were still hundreds of migrants, several more still flying in from the desert, and we found several species we didn't have in the morning.   Also saw 1 hybrid Eur Collared-Dove X Mourning Dove but could not determine how to enter this into e-bird.

New Nevada birds for this final day: Sharp-shinned Hawk (Gerry Hawkins only), Sora (Paul Fox only), definitive Anna's Hummingbird, Rose-breasted Grosbeak, and Hooded Oriole (Bob Barnes only). This bird was also raising it wings while it was sitting on the nest. It did this calling and raising its wings for 15 minutes.  The second White-winged Dove was on a branch beside the nest. To find the White-winged Doves, take Homestead Road South to Lakeside Casino and R.V. Resort. Turn right into the parking lot. Take the first right into a parking area here. Get out of the vehicle and walk between the motorhomes to a path. Turn right on the path and listen for one of the birds calling. It really does sound like "Who Cooks for You." In the trees by the water just before you get to the cattails is where I saw these two White-winged Doves about mid-level in the trees. Have to get underneath the tree to see a flimsy nest that appears to be made out of the cattail leaves. It is much like the color of rotten straw.
